**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. **DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**
**July 23, 2025**

**AREA 1: EXECUTIVE BRANCH: POLICY AND ACTIONS**

**Topic 1.1: International Trade & Tariffs**

The Administration is aggressively pursuing its trade agenda, establishing a firm August 1 deadline for new tariffs that the President has stated "will not be extended" [1]. This assertive stance is forcing a rapid response from global trading partners, who are now rushing to finalize deals before the new duties are implemented [2]. Key bilateral agreements are being secured, including a new trade deal with South Korea that sets tariffs at 15% [3]. In a significant structural change to import policy, the Administration has also suspended the de minimis rule that allowed for tariff-free imports under $800 [4]. This move tightens the tariff net and is reported to have a direct financial impact on American consumers [5].

The policy is creating significant international friction. In a direct retaliation, Ontario, Canada, has canceled a major internet infrastructure deal with Starlink as part of the tariff fight [6]. In South America, Brazilian President Lula is signaling a potential "trade showdown" over the tariff threats [7]. While a trade deal was signed with Pakistan aimed at boosting oil reserves and market ties [8], a comprehensive agreement with India remains elusive, presenting a notable challenge for the administration's global trade strategy [9].

**Topic 1.2: Immigration Policy & Enforcement**

The administration has made a landmark move on immigration policy by issuing an "Executive Order on Birthright Citizenship" [1]. To support its enforcement agenda, the Department of Homeland Security has initiated an aggressive recruitment drive for Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE). This campaign reportedly offers substantial incentives, including "$50K signing bonuses, student loan forgiveness and Trump posters" to entice new agents alongside a "patriotism pitch" [2, 3]. As enforcement operations expand, reports indicate that Louisiana has emerged as the administration's "busiest ICE deportation hub" [4]. One report is also circulating that features a recording allegedly contradicting an ICE officer's official claim of assault during an illegal search of a hospital, which may pose a public relations challenge [5].

**Topic 1.3: Foreign Relations & Diplomacy**

Tensions with key allies are escalating. Canada's recent endorsement of a Palestinian state [1] has drawn a sharp response from President Trump, who stated the move makes it "'very hard' to negotiate" a U.S. trade deal and has issued what is being reported as a direct "threat" over the decision [2]. In South America, the administration's decision to sanction the judge who presided over the trial of former Brazilian President Bolsonaro has prompted accusations from critics of an "'attack on Brazilian democracy'" [3]. Broader analysis suggests that what one report calls President Trump’s “frayed relationships with Putin and Netanyahu” are impeding his wider foreign policy goals, creating a complex diplomatic environment [4].

**Topic 1.4: Domestic Economic & Social Policy**

The administration's domestic agenda is advancing on multiple fronts, sparking considerable debate. Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent has publicly characterized new "Trump accounts" as a potential "'backdoor' way to privatize Social Security," confirming a major policy shift is under consideration [1, 2]. On social policy, the administration has taken punitive action against universities, freezing $108 million in federal funding for Duke Health based on accusations of "'systemic racial discrimination'" [3]. While this pressure was applied, Brown University has reportedly negotiated a separate deal with the White House to have its federal funding restored, suggesting a possible model for resolving such disputes [4]. In economic policy, the Federal Reserve has demonstrated its independence by leaving interest rates unchanged, a direct rebuff to public pressure and demands from President Trump for cuts [5].

**AREA 2: THE JEFFREY EPSTEIN CASE: INVESTIGATION & POLITICAL FALLOUT**

**Topic 2.1: Federal Investigation & White House Response**

The Jeffrey Epstein case has re-emerged as a major political crisis, marked by an apparent conflict between the White House and the Department of Justice. Attorney General Pam Bondi has publicly refuted President Trump's assertion that the Epstein files are a "'hoax'" [1]. The President is reportedly facing scrutiny on three simultaneous fronts: his personal history with Epstein in Florida, the circumstances surrounding Epstein's death during his first term in 2019, and allegations of a current DOJ "cover up" [2].

Simultaneously, new details from the DOJ's investigation are intensifying scrutiny of the case's original handling. Prosecutors have informed judges that the grand juries for both Jeffrey Epstein and Ghislaine Maxwell did not hear testimony directly from any victims [3]. Furthermore, DOJ officials have disclosed that the Epstein grand jury transcripts contain testimony from only two witnesses, raising further questions about the scope of the original inquiry [4].

**Topic 2.2: Congressional Conflict & Victim Reactions**

The Epstein case is fueling significant partisan conflict on Capitol Hill. Senate Democrats have announced they are "prepared to sue the Trump administration" to force the release of the Epstein files [1], while in the lower chamber, House Democrats are using procedural tactics to compel "vote after vote" on the issue [2].

Public comments from the President have also drawn sharp rebukes from the families of Epstein's victims. The family of one abuse survivor issued a public plea for the President not to pardon Ghislaine Maxwell, whom their statement called "'a monster who deserves to rot in prison'" [3]. Separately, Virginia Giuffre's family expressed they were "'shocked'" by President Trump's reported Mar-a-Lago comments in which he described her as "'stolen'" [4].

**AREA 3: CONGRESSIONAL ACTIVITY & PARTY POLITICS**

**Topic 3.1: Intra-Party Tensions and Legislative Action**

Tensions are evident between the White House and some congressional Republicans. Following the advancement of a bill to ban stock trading for members of Congress, President Trump publicly derided Senator Josh Hawley (R-MO) as a "'second tier' senator" [1]. That bill is reportedly advancing with what is being described as a "Trump carve-out" [2]. The President's separate attacks on Senate rules concerning judicial appointments have also reportedly "'offended'" Senator Chuck Grassley (R-IA) and caused irritation among other Republican senators, potentially complicating future nominations [3]. In a separate legislative maneuver reflecting current political dynamics, Senator Hawley has proposed a measure to "exclude ‘Biden voters’ from $600 Trump tariff rebate checks" [4].

**Topic 3.2: Congressional Foreign Policy Debates**

U.S. policy toward Israel continues to be a point of sharp contention in Congress. A recent bid by Senate Democrats to block a $675 million arms deal to Israel failed, but it was supported by what reports describe as a "record number" of Democratic senators [1]. Senators Ossoff (D-GA) and Warnock (D-GA) were among those who voted to curb the arms sale, citing the "hunger crisis in Gaza" as their justification [2]. Criticism is also mounting from the progressive wing, with Senator Bernie Sanders (I-VT), in an interview, referring to Israeli Prime Minister Netanyahu as a "'disgusting liar'" [3]. In a notable statement from the other side of the aisle, Representative Marjorie Taylor Greene (R-GA) was reported as being potentially the "first Republican lawmaker to call Gaza war a ‘genocide’" [4]. Reporting indicates that internal Democratic Party strategy remains complex, with one headline noting that while Representative Jasmine Crockett claims to be the "party's future," not everyone in the party agrees [5].

**AREA 4: PUBLIC DISCOURSE & MEDIA LANDSCAPE**

**Topic 4.1: Public Opinion & Political Controversies**

Public opinion surrounding the administration appears fractured and is the subject of conflicting media reports. A new Times poll indicates that "half of Americans think Trump economy getting worse" [1]. In contrast, a columnist for the New York Times, described by another outlet as "anti-Trump," has reportedly admitted that the President is "'much more successful' than expected in his new term [2]. Past political controversies are also being re-litigated in the public square. Former intelligence officials John Brennan and James Clapper have penned an opinion piece to "Set the Record Straight on Russia and 2016" [3], while a competing report alleges that a "whistleblower" from the original probe was "'pressured' by Obama intel officials" to approve the findings against their will [4]. **Topic 1.1: International Trade & Tariffs**

The Administration is aggressively pursuing its trade agenda, establishing a firm August 1 deadline for new tariffs that the President has stated "will not be extended" [1]. This assertive stance is forcing a rapid response from global trading partners, who are now rushing to finalize deals before the new duties are implemented [2]. Key bilateral agreements are being secured, including a new trade deal with South Korea that sets tariffs at 15% [3]. In a significant structural change to import policy, the Administration has also suspended the de minimis rule that allowed for tariff-free imports under $800 [4]. This move tightens the tariff net and is reported to have a direct financial impact on American consumers [5].

The policy is creating significant international friction. In a direct retaliation, Ontario, Canada, has canceled a major internet infrastructure deal with Starlink as part of the tariff fight [6]. In South America, Brazilian President Lula is signaling a potential "trade showdown" over the tariff threats [7]. While a trade deal was signed with Pakistan aimed at boosting oil reserves and market ties [8], a comprehensive agreement with India remains elusive, presenting a notable challenge for the administration's global trade strategy [9].
